*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon"><img src="images/icons/icon3.png" alt="Lightbulb"> Playing Field - Answer Thread</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29038"><blockquote class="postcontent restore ">Answers to questions posted pertaining to the Playing Field.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS2> Particle Scoring Eligibility - Center Vortex Base*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt; Particle Scoring Eligibility - Center Vortex Base</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29271"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8390</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29194#post29194" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">The Playing Field Floor is defined as "The surface of the tiles that make up the base of the Playing Field." From this definition, the black base of the Center Vortex is not part of the Playing Field Floor.<br><br>&lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt; says in part "After Scoring, Particles must make contact with the Playing Field Floor before they are eligible to be Scored again."<br><br><b>Question:</b> May robots pick up Particles from the black base of the Center Vortex and score them without violating &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt; or must the Particles touch a floor tile first?  In other words, should the black base be considered part of the Playing Field Floor for purposes of &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt; or not?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Great question! <i>Robots</i> may collect <i>Particles</i> from the <i>Center Vortex Base</i> and legally <i>Score</i> them without violating rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Vision Patterns Underneath Beacons*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Vision Patterns Underneath Beacons</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29399"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC7171</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29339#post29339" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Please clarify what the vision patterns under the beacon are for. Also, will they be same for all competitions?<br><br>Thank you.</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> <i>Teams</i> may use the <i>Robot Controller</i> Android device camera in conjunction with Vuforia navigation software, which is part of the default software application library for the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge, to determine the <i>Robot's</i> location on the <i>Playing Field</i> when at least one of the Vision Targets is viewed by the camera. This information will help a <i>Robot</i> navigate to a <i>Beacon</i> location during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>.<br><br>The four images in Appendix B of the Game Manual Part 2 will be used at all competitions and they will always be in the same locations on the <i>Playing Field</i>. See the "Field Setup and Configuration Guide" for the locations of the Vision Targets.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS2> Particle Scoring Eligibility & Game Manual Part 1 Section 5.3.1*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt; Particle Scoring Eligibility &amp; Game Manual Part 1 Section 5.3.1</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29042"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">Section 5.3.1 of the Game Manual Part 1 asks teams to reflect on their <i>Robot's design and the question: ï¿½If everybody did this, would the game play be impossible? If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period Beacon: Triggering the Beacon Button Multiple Times*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period Beacon: Triggering the Beacon Button Multiple Times</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29272"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC4211</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29201#post29201" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is the robot allowed to press the Beacon Button twice in the Autonomous period in order to correct a mistake? Thanks!</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Yes, the action described is allowed. There is no rule that limits the number of times a <i>Robot</i> may press a <i>Beacon</i> trigger button in the <i>Autonomous</i> and <i>Driver-Controlled</i> <i>Periods</i>.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> To help prevent accidental resetting of a <i>Beacon</i> twice by a button press, there is a built-in five second delay after a button is released before the trigger buttons become active and are able to change the illuminated state of the <i>Beacon</i> again.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period - Robot Scoring Particles From Its Starting Location*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period - Robot Scoring Particles From Its Starting Location</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29398"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC7171</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29338#post29338" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Are robots required to move before throwing particles into the center vortex during the autonomous period?<br><br>Thank you.</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> No, <i>Robots</i> are allowed to launch <i>Particles</i> without moving from their <i>Match</i> starting location.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Pinning, Trapping or Blocking Robots-Access to Beacons in the Autonomous Period*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Pinning, Trapping or Blocking Robots-Access to Beacons in the Autonomous Period</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29429"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8923</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29358#post29358" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> Is it legal for a robot to block the opposing alliance's beacons during the Autonomous Period? We are aware of the rules stating that you may not enter the other side for 10 seconds, and that you may not score the other beacons, but can you block access to them? <br><br><b>Question 2</b>: If not, could your robot intentionally "sweep" the area to push other robots away from their beacons? We ask as we have seen similar defensive play in autonomous play in previous years.<br><br>Thanks!</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> <u>Intentional</u> <i>Blocking</i> of an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> from accessing their <i>Alliance's Beacon</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> violates rule &lt;G16&gt;.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Yes, this is an allowed strategy, provided that the opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> does not become <i>Pinned</i>, <i>Trapped</i>, or <i>Blocked</i>. See rule &lt;G16&gt; for the details.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period - Stoping Game Play Early*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period - Stoping Game Play Early</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29430"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8923</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29361#post29361" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal for drivers to press the stop button on the Driver Station during the Autonomous Period? We realize that teams could strategically stop their robots, but what if the robot starts to cause damage? Are the drivers allowed to prevent damage by stopping the robot midway through the Autonomous Period? Can the drive team ask the referee to be allowed to stop their robot in these kinds of situations?<br><br>Thanks!</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> <i>Drive Teams</i> may not stop game play early during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> for strategic reasons. <i>Drive Teams</i> with the cooperation of either a Referee, Field Technical Advisor, or Field Technical Advisor Assistant may press the stop button on the <i>Driver Station</i> if there is unexpected <i>Robot</i> behavior that has or is very likely to damage another <i>Robot</i>, the <i>Playing Field</i>, or the <i>Robot</i> itself.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2.3 Autonomous Period Particle Scoring and Rule <GS10>*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2.3 Autonomous Period Particle Scoring and Rule &lt;GS10&gt;</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29738"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9915</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29638#post29638" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> During autonomous, if our robot picks up the opposing alliance's particles and shoots them into the center vortex, does it count? There is no way during autonomous to intentionally pick up opposing alliance's particles, it has to be accidental, right?<br><b>Question 2:</b> Is there a penalty if opposing alliance's particles our robot accidentally picked up remain inside our robot when autonomous is ended?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> Yes, <i>Particles</i> <i>Scored</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> into an <i>Alliance</i>-specific <i>Center Vortex</i> earn fifteen points each for the <i>Alliance</i> corresponding to that <i>Vortex,</i> regardless of <i>Particle</i> color and the <i>Alliance</i> <i>Robot</i> that launched the <i>Particle</i>.<br><br>The action described in the question is <i>Controlling</i> an opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> and that violates rule &lt;GS10&gt;. After the first warning, a <i>Major Penalty</i> is assessed and an additional <i>Minor Penalty</i> is assessed for every five seconds that the rule violation persists. The rule applies to intentional and accidental <i>Control</i> of the opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i>.<br><br>Repeated violation of &lt;GS10&gt; could bring the Egragious Behaviour rule ,&lt;G26&gt;, into play for flagrant violation of game rules.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Rule &lt;GS10&gt; is violated in the <i>Autonomous</i> and <i>Driver-Controlled Periods</i> as soon as a <i>Robot Controls</i> the opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i>. There is no "free pass" to <i>Control</i> an opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. Rule &lt;GS10&gt; <i>Penalties</i> will be assessed during the <i>Autonomous</i> <i>Period</i> and continue during the <i>Driver-Controlled</i> <i>Period</i> until the opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> has been released from the <i>Robot</i>.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Turn off the <i>Robot's Particle</i> collection system during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> to avoid violating rule &lt;GS10&gt;.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Access to a Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Access to a Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30017"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9915</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29642#post29642" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> During autonomous, after 10 seconds, is it legal to move our robot to just outside of the white gaffe tape, this still gives opposing alliance's robot enough room to access their beacon from other directions if it's programmed to?<br><br><b>Question 2:</b> During autonomous, after 10 seconds, while our robot is moving towards an opposing alliance's beacon, a few inches away from white gaffe tape line area, collides with opposing alliance's robot, both are stalled afterwards, does it violate blocking, pinning, trapping according rule of G16?<br><br><b>Question 3:</b> During autonomous, after 10 seconds, is it legal to move our robot to the middle of opposing alliance's two beacons? Is this a blocking access scenario?<br><b><br>Question 4:</b> Essentially, the question is which area our robot can move to in the opposing alliance side doesn't violate G16?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1: </b>The action described is legal, if the <i>Robot</i> playing defense is <i>Outside</i> the <i>Area</i> defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide gaffers tape.<br><br><b>Answer 2: </b> The action described is legal, if the <i>Robot</i> playing defense is <i>Outside</i> the <i>Area</i> defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape.<br><br><b>Answer 3:</b> This is a legal strategy, if the <i>Robot</i> playing defense is <i>Outside</i> the <i>Area</i> defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape when an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> attempts to access the <i>Beacon</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 4:</b> It is a &lt;G16&gt; rule violation for <i>Blocking</i>, if a <i>Robot</i> is attempting to access its <i>Alliance's Beacon</i> and an opposing <i>Alliance Robot </i>is <i>Inside</i> the <i>Area</i> defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Triggering the <i>Beacon</i> is a high value achievement during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. The game rules were written to protect <i>Robots</i> that are actively attempting to access their <i>Alliance's Beacons</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. Referees will pay very close attention to <i>Robots</i> that intentionally <i>Pin</i>, <i>Trap</i>, or <i>Block</i> an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> that is actively attempting to access their <i>Alliance's Beacon</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. <i>Robots</i> should stay clear of the soft foam tile containing the white gaffers tape on the opposing <i>Alliance's</i> side of the <i>Playing Field</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2.1 Autonomous Period-Beacon Triggered in Favor of the Opposing Alliance*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2.1 Autonomous Period-Beacon Triggered in Favor of the Opposing Alliance</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30020"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9765</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29886#post29886" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> If, during autonomous, a robot mistakenly activates the wrong color on one of their alliance's beacons, do they still earn an extra particle, or would the other alliance?<br><br>Example: Red alliance mistakenly activates one of their beacons to blue, and blue alliance doesn't score one of their own beacons.  Would the blue alliance receive the particle?  The rule specifies that "the states of all the Claims determines how many bonus Particles are released (up to a maximum of two)")</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> For the example, if the <i>Beacon</i> is illuminated blue at the end of the <i>Autonomous Period</i>, the Blue <i>Alliance</i> will receive one Blue <i>Particle </i>and thirty points for the <i>Beacon</i> triggered in their favor by the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i>.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> <i>Robots</i> may avoid awarding a <i>Particle</i> and points to the opposing <i>Alliance</i> by recognizing that the <i>Beacon</i> was triggered in favor of the opposing <i>Alliance</i> and pressing the button again to change the <i>Beacon</i> color.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2.1 Autonomous Period - Adding Earned Particles to the Playing Field*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2.1 Autonomous Period - Adding Earned Particles to the Playing Field</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30022"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC7655</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29941#post29941" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">1.5.2 Autonomous period summary: "...the bonus Particles, if any, will be introduced onto the field by the Referees by placing them into the corresponding Allianceâs Corner Vortex for the Alliance that earned them so that they roll down one of the Particle Returns."<br><br><b>Question:</b> Is it to be assumed that it will be the decision of the referee as to which of the Particle Returns the new Particles are introduced? The <i>Particle</i> should have an equal likelihood of rolling down the left or right ramp. The intent is that the <i>Particle</i> will be introduced to a random location on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>, subject to the design of the C<i>orner Vortex Particle</i> <i>Return</i> ramps.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.1 Pre-Match - Center Vortex Orientation*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.1 Pre-Match - Center Vortex Orientation</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30556"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC11897</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=30365#post30365" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Can you tell me how the vortex is going to be set up for the beginning of the autonomous round, for example will it be randomized by you, or will it be set up from the previous round? <br><b>Question 2:</b> If they are touching the perimeter, can the robot start at an angle?</div></div></div></div></font><b>Answer 1:</b> <i>Drive Teams</i> place their <i>Robots</i> on the <i>Playing Field</i> with the constraints described in section 1.5.1 of the Game Manual Part 2.<br><b><br>Answer 2:</b> Yes.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G3> and Pre-Match Robot Sizing?*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G3&gt; and Pre-Match Robot Sizing?</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_31106"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#B22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC5037</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=30978#post30978" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">How is rule G3, the robot starting volume constraint, enforced at the start of a match?</div></div></div></div></font><br><br><b>Answer:</b> Routine detailed resizing of robots during match setup should not be a normal part of setup.  Referees will be watching for significant violations. Minor concerns will be addressed by sending the robot back to inspection to be appropriately checked for sizing compliance <b>after </b>the match.<br><br>An 18" stick at the field is an OK tool for verifying significant violations, but realistically should not be used to check for "millimeter" compliance. In all cases, the official measure of size compliance is the sizing cube used during Robot Inspection.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.1e - Pre-Match - Preloading Particles*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.1e - Pre-Match - Preloading Particles</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_31371"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8533</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=31259#post31259" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">Given that Game Manual Part 2 Pre Match Section 1.5.1e states in part;<br>ï¿½Teams within an Alliance are required to pre-position or pre-load a total of three Alliance specific Particles for the Autonomous Period. If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana"><br></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS15> Starting the End Game Achievements Early - Lifting the Cap Ball*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS15&gt; Starting the End Game Achievements Early - Lifting the Cap Ball</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29401"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8923</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29357#post29357" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal to intentionally lift the cap ball during the Driver-Controlled Period for transportation purposes? protection has been used against them (&lt;G17&gt;).</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*The Game Design Committee Updated Post #5*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">The Game Design Committee Updated Post #5</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29613"><blockquote class="postcontent restore ">The Game Design Committee changed the answers in post #5 to correct a discrepancy in the Game Q&amp;A Forum.<br><br>We apologize for introducing a temporary inconsistency in the forum.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Rotating the Center Vortex during the End Game.*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Rotating the Center Vortex during the End Game.</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29704"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9915</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29644#post29644" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal to spin the center vortex while an opposing alliance robot is trying to dump Particles during end game? (1.83 m) above the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS11> Cap Ball Inteference - Center Vortex Rotation Caused By Scoring a Cap Ball*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS11&gt; Cap Ball Interference - Playing Offense versus Playing Defense</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30019"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC2818</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29844#post29844" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">In light of End Game #5 answer: "Answer 1: The action described violates rule &lt;GS11&gt; because it interferes with a <i>Robot that is attempting to <i>Score a <i>Cap Ball."</i></i></i><br><br>I'm concerned about whether teams attempting to cap the center vortex will be penalized by movement of the vortex (by their own robot).<br><br>It's hard to conceive of a method of capping the Center Vortex, that is guaranteed NOT to move it.<br><br><b>Question 1:</b> So, if two teams are both attempting to cap the Vortex, and the vortex is rotated in the process, how/will penalties be assessed?<br><br>To me, this brings up the eternal question of: Intent or Accident?  "Was the vortex movement intentional or accidental " (regardless of the consequence to the opponent). This can be impossible for the refs to know.<br><br><b>Question 2:</b> So...   are teams generally excluded from getting a &lt;GS11&gt; penalty if they are also in possession of a Cap Ball in end game, because that automatically puts them in potential capping mode? Or will refs be put in the position of having to decide intent?<br><br>Thanks.</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> <i>Robots</i> attempting to <i>Scor</i>e a <i>Cap Ball</i> in the <i>Center Vortex</i> are playing offense and are not subject to rule &lt;GS11&gt; constraints/<i>Penalties</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> The referee will make the determination if a <i>Robot</i> is attempting to <i>Score</i> their <i>Alliance's Cap Ball</i> (i.e. playing offense) or interfering with an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> that is attempting to <i>Score</i> a <i>Cap Ball</i> (i.e. playing defense). In general, <i>Robots</i> playing offense will not receive a &lt;GS11&gt; <i>Penalty.</i></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-**-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon"><img src="images/icons/icon3.png" alt="Lightbulb"> Miscellaneous Game Questions - Answer Thread</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29039"><blockquote class="postcontent restore ">Answers to questions posted pertaining to miscellaneous Game Questions.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS2> Particle Scoring Eligibility & Game Manual Part 1 Section 5.3.1*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt; Particle Scoring Eligibility &amp; Game Manual Part 1 Section 5.3.1</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29041"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">Section 5.3.1 of the Game Manual Part 1 asks teams to reflect on their <i>Robot's design and the question: ï¿½If everybody did this, would the game play be impossible? If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana"><br></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Controlling the rotation of the Center Vortex.*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Controlling the rotation of the Center Vortex.</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29184"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10092</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29107#post29107" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal to purposefully control the rotation of the <i>Center</i> <i>Vortex</i>?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Yes, <i>Robots</i> may purposefully <i>Control</i> the rotation of the <i>Center Vortex</i>, provided that no other rules are violated. For example, rules &lt;S1&gt;&lt;S1g&gt;, &lt;G14&gt;, &lt;G15&gt;, and &lt;GS8&gt; constrain how a <i>Robot</i> can legally rotate the <i>Center Vortex</i>. <br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Rule &lt;G14&gt; prevents a <i>Robot</i> from grasping a <i>Game Element</i>. In the context of <i>Controlling</i> the rotation of the <i>Center Vortex</i>, <i>Robot</i> contact with the <i>Center Vortex</i> PVC vertical pole from two or more different directions in the horizontal plane is not allowed. For example, a spinning wheel touching the <i>Center Vortex</i> vertical support is allowed, if it does not damage the PVC vertical pole. Using two or more spinning wheels that interact with the PVC vertical pole from different directions in the horizontal plane violates rule &lt;G14&gt;.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Definitions of Open and Closed Recycling Systems*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Definitions of Open and Closed Recycling Systems</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29214"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10092</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29108#post29108" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> What is the definition of an open recycling system?<br><b>Question 2:</b> What is the definition of a closed recycling system?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> <i>Open Recycling System</i> - All <i>Robots</i> participating in a <i>Match</i> have a reasonable opportunity to interact with <i>Scored Particles</i> that have randomly returned from a <i>Vortex</i> to the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> <i>Closed Recycling System</i> - One or more cycles of (1) <i>Scoring</i>, (2) capturing, and (3) re-<i>Scoring </i>a <i>Particle</i> in a manner that denies the other <i>Robots</i> in a <i>Match</i> an equal opportunity to capture a just <i>Scored Particle</i>. The following videos of prototype <i>Robots</i> are examples of <i>Closed Recycling Systems</i> for the <i>Corner Vortex</i>.<br><br>i) <a href="https://youtu.be/FqhtXVk1eZM?t=5m45s" target="_blank">https://youtu.be/FqhtXVk1eZM?t=5m45s</a> - 5 minutes and 45 seconds into the video.<br>ii) <a href="https://youtu.be/5FPnng5BVdg" target="_blank">https://youtu.be/5FPnng5BVdg</a><br><br><i>Robots</i> or game play strategies that have any of the following characteristics are considered to be using a <i>Closed Recycling System</i>:<br>i)  A <i>Robot</i> created confined area that corrals <i>Scored Particles</i> as they exit a <i>Vortex</i>. This is considered a barrier that restricts access to other <i>Robots</i>.<br><br>ii) A mechanism that reduces the randomness of where<i><i> Scored Particles </i></i>return to the <i><i>Playing Field Floor.</i></i><br><br>iii) <i>Controlling</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> before it contacts the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> or <i>Center Vortex Base</i>.<br><br><b><i>Closed Recycling Systems</i> for <i>Scoring </i><u>any quantity<i> of Particles</i></u> in the <i>Corner Vortex</i> and/or <i>Center Vortex</i> are not allowed.<br><br><i>Alliance Partners</i> giving their permission to use a <i>Closed Recycling System</i> <u>does not</u> make a <i>Closed Recycling System</i> legal.</b><br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Do not parse the game rules and the Game Design Committee's posts in the Game Q&amp;A Forum in an attempt to find a legal ambiguity that justifies a <i>Closed Recycling System</i> for <i>Scoring Particles</i>. The Game Design Committee's intent is simple, <u>all</u> <i>Scored Particles</i> should return without restriction to random locations [subject to the design of the Vortex Particle return mechanisms] on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> and both <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> should have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's</i> just <i>Scored Particles</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G14> Robots Grasping Game Elements - U Shaped Alignment Tool for the Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G14&gt; Robots Grasping Game Elements - U Shaped Alignment Tool for the Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29216"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC3785</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29165#post29165" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">Rule &lt;G14&gt; states that Robots cannot grasp, grab or attach to a Game Element. <br> <br><b>Question:</b> Is a "U shaped" alignment tool thats fits on either side of the Beacon [it might touch the sides of the Beacon] allowed?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Yes, provided that the alignment tool does not damage the <i>Beacon</i> and no other rule is violated. Note that we have a very consistent launcher -- all particles launched from a certain position on the field will follow the same trajectory. Consider a cycle to be the release / scoring of multiple particles that were stored in our robot.<br><br>"Pseudo pseudo closed recycling" (Strategy A): Line up semi-randomly on the field such that particles launched will land somewhere in the center vortex. Given the extreme consistency of our launcher, the particles launched (in a given cycle) will land in the same section of the center vortex and thus land in the same area of the field. However, due to semi-random lineup, the area of the field in which the particles land -- out of seven possible areas -- was not predetermined and will likely differ for each separate cycle.<br><br>"Pseudo closed recycling" (Strategy B): Line up on the field such that particles launched will land in a predetermined section of the center vortex (every cycle will launch to this section) and thus land in the same area of the field, every cycle.<br><br>Thanks for your time.</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Both strategies are allowed. <br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> The Game Design Committee's intent is for <i>Robots</i> to launch, push, place, etc. <i>Particles</i> into a <i>Vortex</i> (<i>Center or Corner Vortex</i>â as appropriate) and then collect the just <i>Scored Particles</i> by driving as needed to the location where the <i>Particles</i> naturally return to the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS10> Controlling or Blocking an Opposing Alliance's Scoring Elements - Particles*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS10&gt; Controlling or Blocking an Opposing Alliance's Scoring Elements - Particles</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29324"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC7785</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29241#post29241" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">In the Game Manual Part 2 it states the following as it relates to scoring particles:<br><br>Particle Scoring â Particles Scored into an Alliance-specific Center Vortex earn five (5) points each for the corresponding Alliance (regardless of Particle color. Particles Scored into the Alliance-specific Corner Vortex earn one (1) point each for the corresponding Alliance (regardless of Particle color).<br><br>The language is similar for both autonomous and driver controlled periods. <br> <br><b>Question:</b> Is this to be read as teams can purposely score any color particle in their corner vortex and/or center vortex (ie, red gathering blue particles to score) or is this meant to address inadvertent scoring only (ie, red throws a red particle into a blue vortex).  We ask for clarification and more specific verbiage indicating that alliances are only allowed to control particles of their alliance color or that alliances can control particles of any color for scoring.<br><br>Thank you.</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Rule &lt;GS10&gt; states that <i>Robots</i> may not <i>Control</i> or <i>Block Access</i> to the opposing <i>Alliance's Cap Ball</i> or <i>Particles</i>. Therefore, <i>Robots</i> cannot legally attempt to <i>Score</i> the opposing <i>Alliance's Scoring Elements</i>.<br><br>The <i>Particle Scoring</i> text from the Game Manual that is referenced in the team's question, allows <i>Robots</i> to intentionally or inadvertently <i>Score</i> their <i>Alliance's Particles</i> in the opposing <i>Alliance's Vortex</i> goals. When counting <i>Scored Particles</i>, the <i>Alliance </i>goal is what matters, not which <i>Alliance's Particle</i> entered the goal.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS1> Controlling/Possessing Particles - Scoring Multiple Particles Together*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS1&gt;&lt;GS1g&gt; Controlling/Possessing Particles - Scoring Multiple Particles Together</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29328"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC11111</strong><a href="showthread.php?s=830de23699ab11d234bc8803b7f4f831&amp;p=29260#post29260" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Are robots allowed to score multiple particles together at the same time? Rule &lt;GS1&gt;&lt;GS1g&gt; allows <i>Robots</i> to <i>Control</i> or <i>Possess</i> any quantity of their <i>Alliance's Particles</i> once the <i>Match</i> begins.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> The question references building an arm to collect <i>Particles</i> and then <i>Score</i> them. If the intent is to use the arm to <i>Score Particles</i> in the <i>Center Vortex</i>, rule &lt;GS8&gt; prevents <i>Robots</i> from extending higher than 29 inches (73.6 cm), except during the <i>End Game</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS15> Starting the End Game Achievements Early - Cap Ball lifted by a Particle*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS15&gt; Starting the End Game Achievements Early - Cap Ball lifted by a Particle</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_32514"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10096</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=32352#post32352" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">We understand that we are allowed to grasp a Cap Ball before the End Game, as long as we are not lifting it.<br><br>We also understand that unintentional Cap Ball bouncing during controlled movement (pushing or pulling) will not be penalized.<br><br><b>Question #1:</b> If we maximize the controlled movement of the Cap Ball prior to End Game, by grasping around it (not under it), as a defensive measure, to prevent other teams from knocking it out, as opposed to loosely controlling it with extending assemblies, and we are clearly not engaging the lift mechanism to lift the Cap Ball, should we be penalized for intentionally starting the End Game early due to the Cap Ball bouncing during controlled movement?<br><br><b>Question #2:</b> If during controlled movement, the Cap Ball lifts off of the mat, due to inadvertently running over a particle should we be penalized for intentionally starting the End Game early?</div></div></div></div></font><br><br><b>Answer #1:</b> This question was previously addressed in the "Driver Controlled Period - Answer Thread" post #5.<br><b><br>Answer #2:</b> A referee watching the <i>Match</i> will determine if the <i>Robot</i> is intentionally or <i>Inadvertently</i> lifting the <i>Cap Ball.</i> Intentionally lifting the <i>Cap Ball</i> before the start of the <i>End Game</i> violates rule &lt;GS15&gt;. When the buzzer first sounds or when the buzzer stops?<br><b>Match example:</b> a blue alliance robot is attempting to change a beacon color, the buzzer sounds and while the buzzer is sounding a beacon is pushed, the beacon flashes and changes from red to blue after the buzzer sounds and/or stops, is the beacon scored as red or blue?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Stopping game play late is addressed in rule &lt;G8&gt;. As stated in the rule, the intent is for <i>Robots</i> to stop playing the game within a reasonable human reaction time following the start of the game sound (i.e. buzzer) signaling the end of the <i>Match</i>. <i>Drive Teams</i> should make their best effort to stop game play immediately when the end of the <i>Match</i> game sound begins. Before the <i>Penalties</i> come into play, referees will use their discretion to give <i>Drive Team</i>s an approximate one second grace period following the conclusion of the game sound signaling the end of the <i>Match</i> for <i>Robots</i> to stop playing the game.<br><br><b>Match Example:</b> The <i>Beacon</i> should be <i>Scored</i> as blue because the button was pressed while the buzzer was sounding. A button press that occurs before the conclusion of the one second grace period following the end of the <i>Match</i> should count as <i>Scored</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30242"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8391</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=30055#post30055" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">Post #5, Answer #2 in the autonomous period answer thread states that it is legal to "'sweep' the area to push other robots away from their beacons," provided that "the opposing Alliance Robot does not become Pinned, Trapped, or Blocked".<br><br>Post #8 in the autonomous period answer thread states that "Robots should stay clear of the soft foam tile containing the white gaffers tape on the opposing Alliance's side of the Playing Field during the Autonomous Period."<br><br>In the Game Manual, Blocking is defined as "Preventing an opposing Alliance Robot from accessing an Area or Alliance specific Game Element for an extended period of time by obstructing ALL paths of travel to the object or Area."<br><br><b>Question:</b> Is it legal for a robot to "sweep" (drive over but not park on) the opposing Alliance's side of the Playing Field (including the area by the beacons) during autonomous after the 10 seconds have passed?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> It is legal for a <i>Robot</i> to drive around <i>Inside</i> the opposing <i>Alliance's</i> <i>Area</i> of the <i>Playing Field</i> after the first ten seconds of the <i>Autonomous Period</i> have elapsed. Keep in mind that all of the rules apply to the <i>Autonomous Period</i> unless the Game Manual or Q&amp;A Forum grants an exception. For example, rule &lt;G16&gt; is violated if the defending <i>Robot</i> is <i>Inside</i> the <i>Area</i> <font color="#333333">defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape at the same time that an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> is approaching their <i>Alliance's</i> <i>Beacon.</i> In this scenario, the defending <i>Robot</i> is <i>Blocking</i> because it is between the opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> and their <i>Alliance's Beacon</i>. A rule &lt;G16&gt; violation can occur if the defending <i>Robot</i> is <i>Parked</i> or moving. "Staying clear of the soft foam tile containing the white gaffers tape" is a guideline that will help to keep a <i>Robot</i> from receiving a <i>Penalty</i> for <i>Blocking</i> access to the opposing <i>Alliance's Beacon</i>.</font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS3> Corner Vortex Scoring Violations - Parking on the Corner Vortex*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS3&gt; Corner Vortex Scoring Violations - Parking on the Corner Vortex</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30812"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9849</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=30746#post30746" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> When parking a robot on the Corner Vortex during the autonomous period, to preclude sliding back down the ramp, is it legal to have one of your robot's wheels parked in the Vortex Bar area where the level changes from the Corner Vortex Ramp to the Particle Return ramp? Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_34392"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10353</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=33961#post33961" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Scenario:</b> During the autonomous period of several matches, a red alliance robot triggers both of their alliance's beacons to the correct color, before driving over to the opposing alliance's side of the field and parking in front of their beacon, inside the protected area. The protected area is the area defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape.<br><br><b>Question 1:</b> Does this violate any rules?<br><br><b>Question 2:</b> Same as the scenario, except the blue alliance robot is in the protected area around the beacon before the red robot arrives. The red alliance robot pushes the blue alliance robot sideways away from the beacon and parks in front of the opposing alliance's beacon. Is this allowed?<br><br><b>Question 3</b>: Same as the scenario, except the blue alliance robot is in the protected area around the beacon before the red robot arrives. The red alliance robot pins the blue alliance robot against the playing field perimeter wall, preventing the blue alliance robot from triggering their beacon.</div></div></div></div></font><br><br><b>Answer 1:</b> The Red <i>Alliance Robot's</i> actions are allowed if a <i>Blue Alliance Robot</i> does not attempt to access the Blue <i>Alliance Beacon</i> that is <i>Blocked</i> by the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i>. Rule &lt;G16&gt; consequences come into play if the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> attempts to access the <i>Blocked Beacon</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Yes, the action is allowed if the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> is not attempting to drive back to access the <i>Beacon</i> while the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> is inside the protected <i>Area</i> in front the <i>Beacon</i>. Rule &lt;G16&gt; is violated if the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> attempts to maneuver back to the <i>Beacon</i> and it is <i>Blocked</i> by a Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> that is <i>In</i> the protected <i>Area</i> in front of the <i>Beacon</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 3:</b> The Red <i>Alliance Robot's</i> actions violate rule &lt;G16&gt; for <i>Pinning</i> if the referee determines that it is a deliberate strategy. The Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> having performed this maneuver during several preceding <i>Matches</i> will influence the referee's determination of the <i>Robot's</i> intended strategy for the current <i>Match</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Blocking Access to an Alliance Specific Game Element & <GS6>*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Blocking Access to an Alliance Specific Game Element &amp; &lt;GS6&gt;</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_34574"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC7592</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=34388#post34388" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">I would like to get some clarification on what constitutes blocking of a beacon for a defensive autonomous routine.  Please note all of these scenarios take place after the 10 second mark.<br><br><b>Question 1</b>: If a red alliance robot on the red alliance side has fully entered the tile with the white line when a blue alliance robot enters the tile with the white line makes contact and pushes and prevents the red alliance from claiming the correct beacon color, is this considered blocking?<br><br><b>Question 2</b>: If the incorrect button in question 1 was pressed due to robot contact, provided nothing else occurs with the beacon, is the beacon claimed for the blue alliance?<br><br><b>Question 3</b>: If a red alliance robot on the red alliance side has not yet entered the tile with the white line when a blue alliance robot that is partially in the tile with the white line makes contact and pushes and prevents the red alliance robot from entering the tile with the white line, is this considered blocking?<br><br><b>Question 4</b>: If a red alliance robot on the red alliance side has partially entered the tile with the white line when a blue alliance robot is moving through the tile with the white line makes contact and pushes and prevents the red alliance robot from fully entering the tile with the white line, is this considered blocking?</div></div></div></div></font><br>A <i>Robot</i> cannot incur a &lt;G16&gt; <i>Penalty</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> unless it is determined by a referee to be part of a deliberate strategy. The defensive <i>Robot's</i> behavior in previous <i>Matches</i> will influence the referee's determination of the <i>Robot's</i> intended strategy for the current <i>Match</i>. It is stated in the post that the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> is executing a "defensive autonomous routine." Therefore, the following answers are based on the referee determining that the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> is intentionally playing defense.<br><b><br>Answer 1:</b> No.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> During the <i>Autonomous Period</i>, the answer depends on which <i>Robot</i> triggered the <i>Beacon</i>. A Red <i>Alliance Beacon</i> triggered by contact with a Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> is counted as <i>Scored</i> based on the illuminated color of the <i>Beacon</i>. A Red <i>Alliance Beaco</i>n triggered by contact with a Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> violates rule &lt;GS6&gt;.<br><br><b>Answer 3:</b> Yes.<br><br><b>Answer 4:</b> A Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> entering the restricted <i>Area</i> around the <i>Beacon</i> before the Red <i>Alliance Robo</i>t attempts to enter the restricted <i>Area</i> is <i>Blocking</i> if the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> attempts to access the <i>Beacon</i>. A Blue <i>Alliance Robo</i>t entering the restricted <i>Area</i> around the <i>Beacon</i> after the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> enters the restricted <i>Area</i> is not <i>Blocking</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_34185"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10353</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=33961#post33961" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Scenario:</b> During the autonomous period of several matches, a red alliance robot triggers both of their alliance's beacons to the correct color, before driving over to the opposing alliance's side of the field and parking in front of their beacon, inside the protected area. The protected area is the area defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape.<br><br><b>Question 1:</b> Does this violate any rules?<br><br><b>Question 2:</b> Same as the scenario, except the blue alliance robot is in the protected area around the beacon before the red robot arrives. The red alliance robot pushes the blue alliance robot sideways away from the beacon and parks in front of the opposing alliance's beacon. Is this allowed?<br><br><b>Question 3</b>: Same as the scenario, except the blue alliance robot is in the protected area around the beacon before the red robot arrives. The red alliance robot pins the blue alliance robot against the playing field perimeter wall, preventing the blue alliance robot from triggering their beacon.</div></div></div></div></font><br><br><b>Answer 1:</b> The Red <i>Alliance Robot's</i> actions are allowed if a <i>Blue Alliance Robot</i> does not attempt to access the Blue <i>Alliance Beacon</i> that is <i>Blocked</i> by the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i>. Rule &lt;G16&gt; consequences come into play if the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> attempts to access the <i>Blocked Beacon</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Yes, the action is allowed if the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> is not attempting to drive back to access the <i>Beacon</i> while the Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> is inside the protected <i>Area</i> in front the <i>Beacon</i>. Rule &lt;G16&gt; is violated if the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> attempts to maneuver back to the <i>Beacon</i> and it is <i>Blocked</i> by a Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> that is <i>In</i> the protected <i>Area</i> in front of the <i>Beacon</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 3:</b> The Red <i>Alliance Robot's</i> actions violate rule &lt;G16&gt; for <i>Pinning</i> if the referee determines that it is a deliberate strategy. The Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> having performed this maneuver during several preceding <i>Matches</i> will influence the referee's determination of the <i>Robot's</i> intended strategy for the current <i>Match</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<S1> Unsafe Robot - Penalty for Speeding and <T21> Team Running During an Event*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;S1&gt;&lt;S1g&gt; Unsafe Robot - Penalty for Speeding and &lt;T21&gt; Team Running During an Event</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_34186"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10841</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=34042#post34042" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Can a team be penalized for speeding?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> The game rules do not specifically restrict <i>Robot</i> speed. If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period Beacon: Triggering the Beacon Button Multiple Times*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2 Autonomous Period Beacon: Triggering the Beacon Button Multiple Times</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29272"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC4211</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29201#post29201" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is the robot allowed to press the Beacon Button twice in the Autonomous period in order to correct a mistake? Can the drive team ask the referee to be allowed to stop their robot in these kinds of situations?<br><br>Thanks!</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> <i>Drive Teams</i> may not stop game play early during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> for strategic reasons. <i>Drive Teams</i> with the cooperation of either a Referee, Field Technical Advisor, or Field Technical Advisor Assistant may press the stop button on the <i>Driver Station</i> if there is unexpected <i>Robot</i> behavior that has or is very likely to damage another <i>Robot</i>, the <i>Playing Field</i>, or the <i>Robot</i> itself.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2.3 Autonomous Period Particle Scoring and Rule <GS10>*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2.3 Autonomous Period Particle Scoring and Rule &lt;GS10&gt;</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29738"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9915</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29638#post29638" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> During autonomous, if our robot picks up the opposing alliance's particles and shoots them into the center vortex, does it count? There is no way during autonomous to intentionally pick up opposing alliance's particles, it has to be accidental, right?<br><b>Question 2:</b> Is there a penalty if opposing alliance's particles our robot accidentally picked up remain inside our robot when autonomous is ended?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> Yes, <i>Particles</i> <i>Scored</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> into an <i>Alliance</i>-specific <i>Center Vortex</i> earn fifteen points each for the <i>Alliance</i> corresponding to that <i>Vortex,</i> regardless of <i>Particle</i> color and the <i>Alliance</i> <i>Robot</i> that launched the <i>Particle</i>.<br><br>The action described in the question is <i>Controlling</i> an opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> and that violates rule &lt;GS10&gt;. After the first warning, a <i>Major Penalty</i> is assessed and an additional <i>Minor Penalty</i> is assessed for every five seconds that the rule violation persists. The rule applies to intentional and accidental <i>Control</i> of the opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i>.<br><br>Repeated violation of &lt;GS10&gt; could bring the Egragious Behaviour rule ,&lt;G26&gt;, into play for flagrant violation of game rules.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Rule &lt;GS10&gt; is violated in the <i>Autonomous</i> and <i>Driver-Controlled Periods</i> as soon as a <i>Robot Controls</i> the opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i>. There is no "free pass" to <i>Control</i> an opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. Rule &lt;GS10&gt; <i>Penalties</i> will be assessed during the <i>Autonomous</i> <i>Period</i> and continue during the <i>Driver-Controlled</i> <i>Period</i> until the opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> has been released from the <i>Robot</i>.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Turn off the <i>Robot's Particle</i> collection system during the <i>Autonomous Period</i> to avoid violating rule &lt;GS10&gt;.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Access to a Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Access to a Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30017"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9915</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29642#post29642" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> During autonomous, after 10 seconds, is it legal to move our robot to just outside of the white gaffe tape, this still gives opposing alliance's robot enough room to access their beacon from other directions if it's programmed to?<br><br><b>Question 2:</b> During autonomous, after 10 seconds, while our robot is moving towards an opposing alliance's beacon, a few inches away from white gaffe tape line area, collides with opposing alliance's robot, both are stalled afterwards, does it violate blocking, pinning, trapping according rule of G16?<br><br><b>Question 3:</b> During autonomous, after 10 seconds, is it legal to move our robot to the middle of opposing alliance's two beacons? The game rules were written to protect <i>Robots</i> that are actively attempting to access their <i>Alliance's Beacons</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. Referees will pay very close attention to <i>Robots</i> that intentionally <i>Pin</i>, <i>Trap</i>, or <i>Block</i> an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> that is actively attempting to access their <i>Alliance's Beacon</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>. <i>Robots</i> should stay clear of the soft foam tile containing the white gaffers tape on the opposing <i>Alliance's</i> side of the <i>Playing Field</i> during the <i>Autonomous Period</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.2.1 Autonomous Period-Beacon Triggered in Favor of the Opposing Alliance*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.2.1 Autonomous Period-Beacon Triggered in Favor of the Opposing Alliance</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30020"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9765</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29886#post29886" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> If, during autonomous, a robot mistakenly activates the wrong color on one of their alliance's beacons, do they still earn an extra particle, or would the other alliance?<br><br>Example: Red alliance mistakenly activates one of their beacons to blue, and blue alliance doesn't score one of their own beacons. The <i>Particle</i> should have an equal likelihood of rolling down the left or right ramp. If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana"><br></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS15> Starting the End Game Achievements Early - Lifting the Cap Ball*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS15&gt; Starting the End Game Achievements Early - Lifting the Cap Ball</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29401"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8923</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29357#post29357" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal to intentionally lift the cap ball during the Driver-Controlled Period for transportation purposes?
