If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana"><br></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana">VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Controlling the rotation of the Center Vortex.*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Controlling the rotation of the Center Vortex.</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29184"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10092</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29107#post29107" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal to purposefully control the rotation of the <i>Center</i> <i>Vortex</i>?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Yes, <i>Robots</i> may purposefully <i>Control</i> the rotation of the <i>Center Vortex</i>, provided that no other rules are violated. For example, rules &lt;S1&gt;&lt;S1g&gt;, &lt;G14&gt;, &lt;G15&gt;, and &lt;GS8&gt; constrain how a <i>Robot</i> can legally rotate the <i>Center Vortex</i>. <br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Rule &lt;G14&gt; prevents a <i>Robot</i> from grasping a <i>Game Element</i>. In the context of <i>Controlling</i> the rotation of the <i>Center Vortex</i>, <i>Robot</i> contact with the <i>Center Vortex</i> PVC vertical pole from two or more different directions in the horizontal plane is not allowed. For example, a spinning wheel touching the <i>Center Vortex</i> vertical support is allowed, if it does not damage the PVC vertical pole. Using two or more spinning wheels that interact with the PVC vertical pole from different directions in the horizontal plane violates rule &lt;G14&gt;.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Definitions of Open and Closed Recycling Systems*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Definitions of Open and Closed Recycling Systems</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29214"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC10092</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29108#post29108" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> What is the definition of an open recycling system?<br><b>Question 2:</b> What is the definition of a closed recycling system?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> <i>Open Recycling System</i> - All <i>Robots</i> participating in a <i>Match</i> have a reasonable opportunity to interact with <i>Scored Particles</i> that have randomly returned from a <i>Vortex</i> to the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> <i>Closed Recycling System</i> - One or more cycles of (1) <i>Scoring</i>, (2) capturing, and (3) re-<i>Scoring </i>a <i>Particle</i> in a manner that denies the other <i>Robots</i> in a <i>Match</i> an equal opportunity to capture a just <i>Scored Particle</i>. The following videos of prototype <i>Robots</i> are examples of <i>Closed Recycling Systems</i> for the <i>Corner Vortex</i>.<br><br>i) <a href="https://youtu.be/FqhtXVk1eZM?t=5m45s" target="_blank">https://youtu.be/FqhtXVk1eZM?t=5m45s</a> - 5 minutes and 45 seconds into the video.<br>ii) <a href="https://youtu.be/5FPnng5BVdg" target="_blank">https://youtu.be/5FPnng5BVdg</a><br><br><i>Robots</i> or game play strategies that have any of the following characteristics are considered to be using a <i>Closed Recycling System</i>:<br>i)  A <i>Robot</i> created confined area that corrals <i>Scored Particles</i> as they exit a <i>Vortex</i>. This is considered a barrier that restricts access to other <i>Robots</i>.<br><br>ii) A mechanism that reduces the randomness of where<i><i> Scored Particles </i></i>return to the <i><i>Playing Field Floor.</i></i><br><br>iii) <i>Controlling</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> before it contacts the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> or <i>Center Vortex Base</i>.<br><br><b><i>Closed Recycling Systems</i> for <i>Scoring </i><u>any quantity<i> of Particles</i></u> in the <i>Corner Vortex</i> and/or <i>Center Vortex</i> are not allowed.<br><br><i>Alliance Partners</i> giving their permission to use a <i>Closed Recycling System</i> <u>does not</u> make a <i>Closed Recycling System</i> legal.</b><br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> Do not parse the game rules and the Game Design Committee's posts in the Game Q&amp;A Forum in an attempt to find a legal ambiguity that justifies a <i>Closed Recycling System</i> for <i>Scoring Particles</i>. The Game Design Committee's intent is simple, <u>all</u> <i>Scored Particles</i> should return without restriction to random locations [subject to the design of the Vortex Particle return mechanisms] on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> and both <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> should have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's</i> just <i>Scored Particles</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G14> Robots Grasping Game Elements - U Shaped Alignment Tool for the Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G14&gt; Robots Grasping Game Elements - U Shaped Alignment Tool for the Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29216"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC3785</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29165#post29165" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">Rule &lt;G14&gt; states that Robots cannot grasp, grab or attach to a Game Element. <br> <br><b>Question:</b> Is a "U shaped" alignment tool thats fits on either side of the Beacon [it might touch the sides of the Beacon] allowed?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Yes, provided that the alignment tool does not damage the <i>Beacon</i> and no other rule is violated. Referees will determine if the <i>Robot</i>-to-<i>Robot</i> contact was inadvertent, intentional, avoidable, etc. and if the damaged <i>Robot</i> was an entanglement or safety risk. Appropriate consequences will be applied based on the <i>Robot</i> behaviors and risk factors. If the entanglement or damage is ruled to be deliberate or chronic, the offending <i>Team</i> will receive a <i>Major Penalty</i> and a <i>Yellow Card</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS10> Controlling or Blocking an Opposing Alliance's Scoring Elements - Particle*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS10&gt; Controlling or Blocking an Opposing Alliance's Scoring Elements - Particle</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_33882"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC3848</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=33782#post33782" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">We seek clarification on &lt;GS10&gt; and the Miscellaneous Game Question - Answer Thread posts #9 and #16.<br> <br><b>Question 1:</b> Are teams allowed to unintentionally and inadvertently possess Opposing Alliance Particles?<br> <br><b>Question 2:</b> Are teams allowed to score those unintentionally and inadvertently possessed Particles in their own Vortex(s) without penalty and with reward?<br><br><b>Scenario</b>: A blue alliance robot launches a blue Particle at the blue Center Vortex. If the answer to the question is yes, the design component is probably not allowed."</i></span></font><br><font color="#232323"><span style="font-family: Verdana"><br>VELOCITY VORTEX is played with <i>Particles</i> that are <i>Scored</i> in goals and recycled back to the <i>Playing Field</i> for continuous game play. The Game Design Committee's intent is for <u>open recycling</u>, where <i>Scored Particles</i> return to random locations on the <i>Playing Field Floor</i> so that <u>both</u> <i>Robots</i> on an <i>Alliance</i> have an equal opportunity to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> their <i>Alliance's Scored Particles</i>. A <u>closed recycling</u> game strategy that denies a reasonable opportunity for an <i>Alliance Partner Robot</i> to access, <i>Control</i>, or <i>Possess</i> a <i>Scored Particle</i> is not in the spirit of the <i>FIRST</i> Tech Challenge and is not allowed. Game play with closed recycling of <i>Particles</i> would be impossible and unfair to <i>Alliance Partners</i>. Therefore, <i>Robot</i> designs and/or game strategies that deny their <i>Alliance Partner</i> equal access to <i>Scored Particles</i>, is considered to be a violation of rule &lt;GS2&gt;&lt;GS2g&gt;.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Section 1.5.4 1c - End Game: Cap Ball On the Center Vortex Base*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Section 1.5.4 1c - End Game: Cap Ball On the Center Vortex Base</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29183"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC5501</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29135#post29135" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">In the End Game, a Robot can lift the Cap Ball off of the Playing Field Floor for points. Their intent is to get out of our way but because they are stuck between us and our alliance partner they have limited space to move which has caused the interference. <br><br><b>Question 2:</b> If we are in the process of lifting the cap ball and the other alliance is trying to push their cap ball up the ramp or clamp on to it but end up pushing it into our robot while we are lifting would that be considered interfering with our lift?<br><br><b>Question 3:</b> In the same scenario as question 2, would it change the penalty if they were still actively pushing the cap ball against us and not just letting the cap ball bounce off of us and move out of our way?</div></div></div></div></font><br><br><b>Answer 1:</b> For the case where the <i>Robot</i> is "collecting the <i>Cap Ball</i>," there are no rule &lt;GS11&gt; consequences for <i>Cap Ball</i> interference because the rule &lt;GS11&gt; protections start when the <i>Cap Ball</i> is lifted off of the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>.<br><br>For the scenario where the <i>Robot</i> has lifted the <i>Cap Ba</i>ll off of the <i>Playing Field Floor</i>, rules &lt;GS11&gt;, &lt;G16&gt;, and &lt;G17&gt; all come into play. First, we need to identify each robot: Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> 1 is lifting their A<i>lliance's Cap Ball</i>, Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> 2 is playing defense, and the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> is between the two Red <i>Alliance Robots</i>. Here is the call:<br><br>a) The Red <i>Alliance Robots</i> are violating rule &lt;G16&gt; for <i>Pinning</i> the Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i>.<br>b) The Blue <i>Alliance Robo</i>t should not incur &lt;GS11&gt; consequences for attempting to drive away from the Red <i>Alliance Robots</i> because it is protected by rule &lt;G17&gt; while it is <i>Pinned</i> by the Red <i>Alliance Robots</i>.<br>c) The Red <i>Alliance Robots</i> need to stop <i>Pinning</i> the Blue <i>Alliance Robot. </i>The Blue <i>Alliance Robot</i> should break contact with Red <i>Alliance Robot</i> 1 when the <i>Pinning</i> situation ends.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Rule &lt;GS11&gt; consequences should not come into play if both <i>Robots</i> are playing offense with a <i>Cap Ball</i>. Rule &lt;GS11&gt; consequences should come into play if one of the <i>Robots</i> is using a <i>Cap Ball</i> as part of a defensive strategy.<br><br><b>Answer 3:</b> A <i>Robot</i> may not use &lt;GS11&gt; protections to gain a defensive advantage over the opposing <i>Alliance</i>. The <i>Robot</i> that is intentionally pushing their <i>Alliance's Cap Ball</i> against an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> that is in the act of lifting their<i> Alliance's Cap Ball</i> is subject to rule &lt;GS11&gt; consequences.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS11> Cap Ball Interference*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS11&gt; Cap Ball Interference</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_34189"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC4628</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=34089#post34089" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">During endgame, team A is up against a wall trying to pick up a particle. When the buzzer first sounds or when the buzzer stops?<br><b>Match example:</b> a blue alliance robot is attempting to change a beacon color, the buzzer sounds and while the buzzer is sounding a beacon is pushed, the beacon flashes and changes from red to blue after the buzzer sounds and/or stops, is the beacon scored as red or blue?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Stopping game play late is addressed in rule &lt;G8&gt;. As stated in the rule, the intent is for <i>Robots</i> to stop playing the game within a reasonable human reaction time following the start of the game sound (i.e. buzzer) signaling the end of the <i>Match</i>. <i>Drive Teams</i> should make their best effort to stop game play immediately when the end of the <i>Match</i> game sound begins. Before the <i>Penalties</i> come into play, referees will use their discretion to give <i>Drive Team</i>s an approximate one second grace period following the conclusion of the game sound signaling the end of the <i>Match</i> for <i>Robots</i> to stop playing the game.<br><br><b>Match Example:</b> The <i>Beacon</i> should be <i>Scored</i> as blue because the button was pressed while the buzzer was sounding. A button press that occurs before the conclusion of the one second grace period following the end of the <i>Match</i> should count as <i>Scored</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<G16> Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;G16&gt; Pinning, Trapping, or Blocking Robots - Blocking Access to a Beacon</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30242"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC8391</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=30055#post30055" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">Post #5, Answer #2 in the autonomous period answer thread states that it is legal to "'sweep' the area to push other robots away from their beacons," provided that "the opposing Alliance Robot does not become Pinned, Trapped, or Blocked".<br><br>Post #8 in the autonomous period answer thread states that "Robots should stay clear of the soft foam tile containing the white gaffers tape on the opposing Alliance's side of the Playing Field during the Autonomous Period."<br><br>In the Game Manual, Blocking is defined as "Preventing an opposing Alliance Robot from accessing an Area or Alliance specific Game Element for an extended period of time by obstructing ALL paths of travel to the object or Area."<br><br><b>Question:</b> Is it legal for a robot to "sweep" (drive over but not park on) the opposing Alliance's side of the Playing Field (including the area by the beacons) during autonomous after the 10 seconds have passed?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> It is legal for a <i>Robot</i> to drive around <i>Inside</i> the opposing <i>Alliance's</i> <i>Area</i> of the <i>Playing Field</i> after the first ten seconds of the <i>Autonomous Period</i> have elapsed. Keep in mind that all of the rules apply to the <i>Autonomous Period</i> unless the Game Manual or Q&amp;A Forum grants an exception. For example, rule &lt;G16&gt; is violated if the defending <i>Robot</i> is <i>Inside</i> the <i>Area</i> <font color="#333333">defined by the soft foam floor tile (not including the tile connecting teeth) that contains the one-inch-wide strip of white gaffers tape at the same time that an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> is approaching their <i>Alliance's</i> <i>Beacon.</i> In this scenario, the defending <i>Robot</i> is <i>Blocking</i> because it is between the opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> and their <i>Alliance's Beacon</i>. A rule &lt;G16&gt; violation can occur if the defending <i>Robot</i> is <i>Parked</i> or moving. "Staying clear of the soft foam tile containing the white gaffers tape" is a guideline that will help to keep a <i>Robot</i> from receiving a <i>Penalty</i> for <i>Blocking</i> access to the opposing <i>Alliance's Beacon</i>.</font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<GS3> Corner Vortex Scoring Violations - Parking on the Corner Vortex*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;GS3&gt; Corner Vortex Scoring Violations - Parking on the Corner Vortex</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_30812"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9849</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=30746#post30746" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> When parking a robot on the Corner Vortex during the autonomous period, to preclude sliding back down the ramp, is it legal to have one of your robot's wheels parked in the Vortex Bar area where the level changes from the Corner Vortex Ramp to the Particle Return ramp? Controlling or Blocking an Opposing Alliance's Scoring Elements - Particle</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29516"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC5414</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29445#post29445" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question 1:</b> If an particle belonging to the opposing alliance drops from the center vortex and lands on top of an opposing alliance, becoming lodged in or on the robot, will this be considered a penalty for controlling a particle of the opposing alliance? <br> <br><b>Question 2:</b> If it is a penalty, will the team controlling the particle be continually called for penalties until they remove the particle from their robot? <br> <br><b>Question 3:</b> If the answer to both of these questions is yes, then can the offending team disable their robot to avoid receiving additional penalties.<br><br>Thanks.</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer 1:</b> Yes, this violates rule &lt;GS10&gt;. Keeping an opposing <i>Alliance's Particle</i> out of play creates a significant competitive advantage.<br><br><b>Answer 2:</b> Yes, <i>Penalties</i> will be assessed as described in rule &lt;GS10&gt;.<br><br><b>Answer 3:</b> No, rule &lt;G23&gt; does not protect a <i>Robot</i> from earring <i>Penalties</i> when it is <i>Disabled</i> for strategic reasons.<br><br><b>Tip from the Game Design Committee:</b> <i>Robots</i> should be designed to prevent unintentional <i>Possession</i> of the opposing <i>Alliance's Particles</i>.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Can the GDC describe a "legal" way to recover particles from the corner vortex?*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Can the GDC describe a "legal" way to recover particles from the corner vortex?</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29517"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9765</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29457#post29457" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> As there are a limited number of possible return paths for a particle that has been scored in the corner vortex, can you define a legal distance that the particle must travel on the floor, or a set time that the particle must be avoided, or a minimum distance that our robot must stay back from the particle return, so that retrieving this particle would be considered "open recycling?"</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> No, adding the suggested parameters introduces rule loopholes that could allow <i>Robots</i> to defeat the Game Design Committee's intent for how to legally recycle <i>Particles</i> during game play.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*<RG08> Launching Game Scoring Elements - Trajectory Constraints For Particles*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">&lt;RG08&gt; Launching Game Scoring Elements - Trajectory Constraints For Particles</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29618"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9779</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29554#post29554" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message">Game Manual Part 1 rule &lt;RG08&gt; states:<br><br>Robots are allowed to launch game Scoring Elements through the air. It is expected that Teams will launch the elements with just enough velocity to score. If the referees feel that a Robot is launching Scoring Elements with excessive velocity that would cause a safety issue if they were to leave the field the Robot will be required to be inspected. Robots must then demonstrate that a launched Game Element cannot travel in the air more than a distance of 4.88 m (16 ft.) or more than 1.83 m (6 ft.) in elevation.<br><br><b>Question:</b><br>The wording of this rule seems to indicate that it is perfectly legal to launch particles in excess of the maximum 16 feet distance and 6 feet elevation, as long as the referees feel that the launching of the particles is responsible and does not pose any safety issues. Our team currently launch particles nearly straight up from under the center vortex. At the top of the slow arch, the ball reaches a height of 6 feet 6 inches. We just want to clarify the intent of the game design committee in regards to this rule.<br><br>Thank you.</div></div></div></div></font><br><font color="#3E3E3E"><span style="font-family: Verdana"><b>Answer:</b> The Game Design Committee's intent is for a launched <i>Particle</i> to travel in the air no more than a distance of 4.88 m (16 ft.) and/or no more than 1.83 m (6 ft.) in elevation. <i>Robots</i> may not legally launch <i>Particles</i> further or higher than these limits.</span></font></blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*Pushing an opposing Alliance Robot while it is launching Particles.*-1THEREDDKING-*<div class="postrow"><h2 class="title icon">Pushing an opposing Alliance Robot while it is launching Particles.</h2><div class="content"><div id="post_message_29703"><blockquote class="postcontent restore "><font color="#b22222"><div class="bbcode_container"><div class="bbcode_quote"><div class="quote_container"><div class="bbcode_quote_container"></div><div class="bbcode_postedby"><img src="images/misc/quote_icon.png" alt="Quote"> Originally Posted by <strong>FTC9915</strong><a href="showthread.php?p=29643#post29643" rel="nofollow"><img class="inlineimg" src="images/buttons/viewpost-right.png" alt="View Post"></a></div><div class="message"><b>Question:</b> Is it legal to push an opposing alliance robot while it's launching particles into the center vortex?</div></div></div></div></font><br><b>Answer:</b> Yes, provided that no other rule is violated. For example, <i>Drive Teams</i> using aggressive actions against an opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> should have a clear understanding of the Unsafe <i>Robot</i> and and <i>Playing Field</i> <i>Damage</i> rule, &lt;S1&gt;&lt;S1g&gt;. If the opposing <i>Alliance Robot</i> is launching <i>Particles</i> towards a <i>Vortex</i>, the <i>Particle</i> interference rule &lt;GS9&gt; could come into play. <i>Drive Teams</i> should also be careful not to violate the <i>Pinning</i>, <i>Trapping</i>, or <i>Blocking Robots</i> rule, &lt;G16&gt;.</blockquote></div></div></div>*-THEREDDKING-*
